      <p><b>Burkina Faso</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Burkina_Faso.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/En-us-Burkina_Faso.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Burkina Faso.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <small>French:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[buʁkina faso]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> that covers an area of around 274,200 square kilometres (105,900&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to the southwest. The July 2019 population estimate by the United Nations was 20,321,378.<sup id="cite_ref-worldpopulationreview.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldpopulationreview.com-10">[10]</a></sup> Previously called <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a> (1958–1984), it was <a href="/wiki/Geographical_renaming" title="Geographical renaming">renamed</a> "Burkina Faso" on 4 August 1984 by President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>. Its citizens are known as <i>Burkinabé</i> or <i>Burkinabè</i> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">bur-<span style="font-size:90%">KEE</span>-nə-bay</i></a>), and its capital is <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>. Due to <a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French colonialism</a>, the country's official language of government and business is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, but this language is spoken by approximately only 10–15% of the population. There are 59 native languages spoken in Burkina, with the most common language, <a href="/wiki/Mossi_language" title="Mossi language">Moore</a>, spoken by roughly 50% of Burkinabé.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIAWorldFactBook2020_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWorldFactBook2020-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a> was established on 11 December 1958 as a <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colony</a> within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a> and on 5 August 1960 it gained full independence with <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo" title="Maurice Yaméogo">Maurice Yaméogo</a> as <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Burkina_Faso" title="List of heads of state of Burkina Faso">President</a>. After protests by students and labour union members, Yaméogo was deposed in the <a href="/wiki/1966_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1966 Upper Voltan coup d'état">1966 coup d'état</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Sangoul%C3%A9_Lamizana" title="Sangoulé Lamizana">Sangoulé Lamizana</a>, who became president. His rule coincided with the <a href="/wiki/Sahel_drought" title="Sahel drought">Sahel drought</a> and famine, and facing problems from the country's trade unions he was deposed in the <a href="/wiki/1980_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Upper Voltan coup d'état">1980 coup d'état</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Saye_Zerbo" title="Saye Zerbo">Saye Zerbo</a>. Encountering resistance from trade unions again, Zerbo's government was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/1982_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1982 Upper Voltan coup d'état">1982 coup d'état</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Ou%C3%A9draogo" title="Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo">Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo</a>. </p>
      <p>The leader of the leftist faction of Ouédraogo's government, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>, was made <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Burkina Faso">Prime Minister</a> but was later imprisoned. Efforts to free him led to the 1983 coup d'état, in which he became president.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersChe2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersChe2-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup> Sankara renamed the country Burkina Faso and launched an ambitious socioeconomic programme which included a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> campaign, <a href="/wiki/Land_redistribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Land redistribution">land redistribution</a> to peasants, railway and road construction and the outlawing of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grila2_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grila2-15">[15]</a></sup> Sankara was overthrown and killed in the <a href="/wiki/1987_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1987 Burkinabé coup d'état">1987 coup d'état</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a> – deteriorating relations with former coloniser France and its ally the Ivory Coast were the reason given for the coup. </p>
      <p>In 1987, Blaise Compaoré became president and, after an alleged <a href="/wiki/1989_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1989 Burkinabé coup d'état attempt">1989 coup attempt</a>, was later elected in <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_1991" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 1991">1991</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_1998" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 1998">1998</a>, elections which were boycotted by the opposition and received a considerably low turnout, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 2005">2005</a>. He remained head of state until he was ousted from power by the <a href="/wiki/2014_Burkinab%C3%A9_uprising" title="2014 Burkinabé uprising">popular youth upheaval of 31 October 2014</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> after which he was exiled to the Ivory Coast. <a href="/wiki/Michel_Kafando" title="Michel Kafando">Michel Kafando</a> subsequently became the transitional president of the country. On 16 September 2015, <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2015 Burkinabé coup d'état">a military coup d'état</a> against the Kafando government was carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_of_Presidential_Security" title="Regiment of Presidential Security">Regiment of Presidential Security</a>, the former presidential guard of Compaoré.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyTelegraph_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyTelegraph-18">[18]</a></sup> On 24 September 2015, after pressure from the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/ECOWAS" class="mw-redirect" title="ECOWAS">ECOWAS</a> and the armed forces, the military junta agreed to step down and Michel Kafando was reinstated as acting president.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_World_News_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_World_News-19">[19]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_general_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé general election, 2015">general election held on 29 November 2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roch_Marc_Christian_Kabor%C3%A9" title="Roch Marc Christian Kaboré">Roch Marc Christian Kaboré</a> won in the first round with 53.5% of the vote<sup id="cite_ref-Kabore_wins_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kabore_wins-20">[20]</a></sup> and was sworn in as president on 29 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-swears_in_new_president_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swears_in_new_president-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Government_and_politics"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Government and politics</span></a> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Constitution"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Constitution</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Formerly called the Republic of Upper Volta, the country was renamed "Burkina Faso" on 4 August 1984 by then-President Thomas Sankara. The words "Burkina" and "Faso" both stem from different languages spoken in the country: "Burkina" comes from <a href="/wiki/Mossi_language" title="Mossi language">Mossi</a> and means "upright", showing how the people are proud of their integrity, while "Faso" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Dioula_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioula language">Dioula language</a> (as written in <a href="/wiki/N%27Ko_script" title="N'Ko script">N'Ko</a>: <span lang="dyu" dir="rtl" title="Dyula-language text">ߝߊ߬ߛߏ߫</span>‎ <i>faso</i>) and means "fatherland" (literally, "father's house"). The "-bè" suffix added onto "Burkina" to form the demonym "Burkinabè" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula language</a> and means "men or women".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The CIA summarizes the etymology as "land of the honest (incorruptible) men".<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French colony of Upper Volta was named for its location on the upper courses of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta River</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White Volta</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Burkina_Faso" title="History of Burkina Faso">History of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The northwestern part of present-day Burkina Faso was populated by <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> from 14000 BCE to 5000 BCE. Their tools, including <a href="/wiki/Scraper_(archaeology)" title="Scraper (archaeology)">scrapers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chisel" title="Chisel">chisels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arrowhead" title="Arrowhead">arrowheads</a>, were discovered in 1973 through <a href="/wiki/Excavation_(archaeology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Excavation (archaeology)">archaeological excavations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">[25]</a></sup> Agricultural settlements were established between 3600 and 2600&nbsp;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bura_culture" title="Bura culture">Bura culture</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron-Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a> centred in the southwest portion of modern-day Niger and in the southeast part of contemporary Burkina Faso.<sup id="cite_ref-whc.unesco.org_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whc.unesco.org-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iron_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Iron industry">Iron industry</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forging</a> for tools and weapons, had developed in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> by 1200&nbsp;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> From the 3rd to the 13th centuries CE, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Bura_culture" title="Bura culture">Bura culture</a> existed in the territory of present-day southeastern Burkina Faso and southwestern Niger. Various ethnic groups of present-day Burkina Faso, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Mossi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dyula_people" title="Dyula people">Dioula</a>, arrived in successive waves between the 8th and 15th centuries. From the 11th century, the Mossi people established <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Kingdoms" title="Mossi Kingdoms">several separate kingdoms</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg/350px-Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg/525px-Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg/700px-Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1588" data-file-height="771"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Africa_de_l%27O%C3%A8st_en_1875-es.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>West Africa circa 1875
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1890s, during the European <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, the territory of Burkina Faso was invaded by <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, and colonial control was established following a war of conquest between 1896 and 1904. The territory was made part of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> in 1904, and the colony of <a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French Upper Volta</a> was established on 1 March 1919. The colony was named for its location on the upper courses of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta River</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White Volta</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="8th_century_to_18th_century">8th century to 18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 8th century to 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Historians began to debate about the exact dates when Burkina Faso's many ethnic groups arrived to the area. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moosei_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moosei people (page does not exist)">Proto-Mossi</a> arrived in the far Eastern part of what is today Burkina Faso sometime between the 8th and 11th centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Samo_language_(Burkina)" title="Samo language (Burkina)">Samo</a> arrived around the 15th century,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-30">[30]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dogon_people" title="Dogon people">Dogon</a> lived in Burkina Faso's north and northwest regions until sometime in the 15th or 16th centuries<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and many of the other ethnic groups that make up the country's population arrived in the region during this time. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MossiCavalry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg/220px-MossiCavalry.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg/330px-MossiCavalry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MossiCavalry.jpg/440px-MossiCavalry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1042"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MossiCavalry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The cavalry of the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_Kingdoms" title="Mossi Kingdoms">Mossi Kingdoms</a> were experts at raiding deep into enemy territory, even against the formidable <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/220px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/330px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg/440px-Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2325" data-file-height="1693"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pg381_Des_hommes_sur_les_toits_s%27opposent.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Armed men prevent the French explorer <a href="/wiki/Louis-Gustave_Binger" title="Louis-Gustave Binger">Louis-Gustave Binger</a> from entering Sia (Bobo-Dioulasso) during his stay in April 1892.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> the Mossi established several separate kingdoms including those of Tenkodogo, Yatenga, Zandoma, and Ouagadougou.<sup id="cite_ref-Nations_2014_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nations_2014-32">[32]</a></sup> Sometime between 1328 and 1338 Mossi warriors raided <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> but the Mossi were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Sonni_Ali" title="Sonni Ali">Sonni Ali</a> of <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai</a> at the Battle of Kobi in Mali in 1483.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the early 16th century the Songhai conducted many slave raids into what is today Burkina Faso.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-30">[30]</a></sup> During the 18th century the Gwiriko Empire was established at <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect" title="Bobo Dioulasso">Bobo Dioulasso</a> and ethnic groups such as the Dyan, Lobi, and Birifor settled along the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black Volta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="From_colony_to_independence_.281890s.E2.80.931958.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="From_colony_to_independence_(1890s–1958)">From colony to independence (1890s–1958)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: From colony to independence (1890s–1958)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Upper_Senegal_and_Niger" title="Upper Senegal and Niger">Upper Senegal and Niger</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French Upper Volta</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Starting in the early 1890s a series of European military officers made attempts to claim parts of what is today Burkina Faso. At times these <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialists</a> and their armies fought the local peoples; at times they forged alliances with them and made treaties. The colonialist officers and their home governments also made treaties amongst themselves. Through a complex series of events what is today Burkina Faso eventually became a <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French protectorate</a> in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:French_West_Africa_1913_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/French_West_Africa_1913_map.png/220px-French_West_Africa_1913_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/French_West_Africa_1913_map.png/330px-French_West_Africa_1913_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/French_West_Africa_1913_map.png 2x" data-file-width="440" data-file-height="363"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:French_West_Africa_1913_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> circa 1913
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The eastern and western regions, where a standoff against the forces of the powerful ruler <a href="/wiki/Samori_Ture" title="Samori Ture">Samori Ture</a> complicated the situation, came under French occupation in 1897. By 1898, the majority of the territory corresponding to Burkina Faso was nominally conquered; however, French control of many parts remained uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_Convention_of_1898" title="Anglo-French Convention of 1898">Franco-British Convention of 14 June 1898</a> created the country's modern borders. In the French territory, a war of conquest against local communities and political powers continued for about five years. In 1904, the largely pacified territories of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta basin</a> were integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Senegal_and_Niger" title="Upper Senegal and Niger">Upper Senegal and Niger</a> colony of <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> as part of the reorganization of the French West African colonial empire. The colony had its capital in <a href="/wiki/Bamako" title="Bamako">Bamako</a>. </p>
      <p>The language of colonial administration and schooling became French. The public education system started from humble origins. Advanced education was provided for many years during the colonial period in Dakar. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">Draftees</a> from the territory participated in the European fronts of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in the battalions of the <a href="/wiki/Tirailleurs_s%C3%A9n%C3%A9galais" class="mw-redirect" title="Tirailleurs sénégalais">Senegalese Rifles</a>. Between 1915 and 1916, the districts in the western part of what is now Burkina Faso and the bordering eastern fringe of Mali became the stage of one of the most important armed oppositions to colonial government: the <a href="/wiki/Volta-Bani_War" title="Volta-Bani War">Volta-Bani War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French government finally suppressed the movement but only after suffering defeats. It also had to organize its largest expeditionary force of its colonial history to send into the country to suppress the insurrection. Armed opposition wracked the Sahelian north when the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> and allied groups of the Dori region ended their truce with the government. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/220px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/330px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg/440px-Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="788"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mittelholzer-ouagadougou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The capital, <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, in 1930
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/French_Upper_Volta" title="French Upper Volta">French Upper Volta</a> was established on 1 March 1919. The French feared a recurrence of armed uprising and had related economic considerations. To bolster its administration, the colonial government separated the present territory of Burkina Faso from Upper Senegal and Niger. </p>
      <p>The new colony was named <i>Haute Volta,</i> and François Charles Alexis Édouard Hesling became its first <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Upper_Volta" class="mw-redirect" title="List of governors of Upper Volta">governor</a>. Hesling initiated an ambitious road-making program to improve infrastructure and promoted the growth of cotton for export. The cotton policy – based on <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a> – failed, and revenue generated by the colony stagnated. The colony was dismantled on 5 September 1932, being split between the French colonies of <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">French Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>. Ivory Coast received the largest share, which contained most of the population as well as the cities of Ouagadougou and Bobo-Dioulasso. </p>
      <p>France reversed this change during the period of intense anti-colonial agitation that followed the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. On 4 September 1947, it revived the colony of Upper Volta, with its previous boundaries, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>. The French designated its colonies as departments of <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan France</a> on the European continent. </p>
      <p>On 11 December 1958 the colony achieved <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-government</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a>; it joined the Franco-African Community. A revision in the organization of French Overseas Territories had begun with the passage of the Basic Law (Loi Cadre) of 23 July 1956. This act was followed by reorganization measures approved by the French parliament early in 1957 to ensure a large degree of self-government for individual territories. Upper Volta became an autonomous republic in the French community on 11 December 1958. Full independence from France was received in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL1-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Upper_Volta_.281958.E2.80.931984.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Volta_(1958–1984)">Upper Volta (1958–1984)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Upper Volta (1958–1984)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg/220px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg/330px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg/440px-Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4171" data-file-height="2988"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo_and_Louis_Jacquinot_exchanging_instruments_of_ratification_for_the_independence_of_the_Upper_Volta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo" title="Maurice Yaméogo">Maurice Yaméogo</a>, the first President of Upper Volta, examines documents pertaining to the ratification of the country's independence in 1960
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Republic of Upper Volta</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of Upper Volta (French: <i lang="fr">République de Haute-Volta</i>) was established on 11 December 1958 as a <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colony</a> within the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>. The name <i>Upper Volta</i> related to the nation's location along the upper reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Volta_River" title="Volta River">Volta River</a>. The river's three <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> are called the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red Volta</a>. These were expressed in the three colors of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Upper_Volta" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of Upper Volta">former national flag</a>. </p>
      <p>Before attaining autonomy, it had been French Upper Volta and part of the French Union. On 5 August 1960, it attained full independence from <a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic">France</a>. The first president, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Yam%C3%A9ogo" title="Maurice Yaméogo">Maurice Yaméogo</a>, was the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Voltaic_Democratic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Voltaic Democratic Union">Voltaic Democratic Union</a> (UDV). The 1960 constitution provided for election by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> of a president and a national assembly for five-year terms. Soon after coming to power, Yaméogo banned all political parties other than the UDV. The government lasted until 1966. After much unrest, including mass demonstrations and strikes by students, labor unions, and civil servants, the military intervened. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Lamizana.27s_rule_and_multiple_coups"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lamizana's_rule_and_multiple_coups">Lamizana's rule and multiple coups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Lamizana's rule and multiple coups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/1966_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1966 Upper Voltan coup d'état">1966 military coup</a> deposed Yaméogo, suspended the constitution, dissolved the National Assembly, and placed Lt. Col. <a href="/wiki/Sangoul%C3%A9_Lamizana" title="Sangoulé Lamizana">Sangoulé Lamizana</a> at the head of a government of senior army officers. The army remained in power for four years. On 14 June 1976, the Voltans ratified a new constitution that established a four-year transition period toward complete civilian rule. Lamizana remained in power throughout the 1970s as president of military or mixed civil-military governments. Lamizana's rule coincided with the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Sahel_drought" title="Sahel drought">Sahel drought</a> and famine which had a devastating impact on Upper Volta and neighboring countries. After conflict over the 1976 constitution, a new constitution was written and approved in 1977. Lamizana was re-elected by open elections in 1978. </p>
      <p>Lamizana's government faced problems with the country's traditionally powerful trade unions, and on 25 November 1980, Col. <a href="/wiki/Saye_Zerbo" title="Saye Zerbo">Saye Zerbo</a> overthrew President Lamizana in a <a href="/wiki/1980_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Upper Voltan coup d'état">bloodless coup</a>. Colonel Zerbo established the Military Committee of Recovery for National Progress as the supreme governmental authority, thus eradicating the 1977 constitution. </p>
      <p>Colonel Zerbo also encountered resistance from trade unions and was overthrown two years later by Maj. Dr. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Ou%C3%A9draogo" title="Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo">Jean-Baptiste Ouédraogo</a> and the Council of Popular Salvation (CSP) in the <a href="/wiki/1982_Upper_Voltan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1982 Upper Voltan coup d'état">1982 Upper Voltan coup d'état</a>. The CSP continued to ban political parties and organizations, yet promised a transition to civilian rule and a new constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="1983_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1983_coup_d'état">1983 coup d'état</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1983 coup d'état">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Infighting developed between the right and left factions of the CSP. The leader of the leftists, Capt. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>, was appointed prime minister in January 1983, but subsequently arrested. Efforts to free him, directed by Capt. <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9" title="Blaise Compaoré">Blaise Compaoré</a>, resulted in a military coup d'état on 4 August 1983. </p>
      <p>The coup brought Sankara to power and his government began to implement a series of revolutionary programs which included mass-vaccinations, infrastructure improvements, the expansion of women's rights, encouragement of domestic agricultural consumption, and anti-desertification projects.<sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Burkina_Faso_.28since_1984.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Burkina_Faso_(since_1984)">Burkina Faso (since 1984)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Burkina Faso (since 1984)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         <th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th>

      <p>On 2 August 1984, on President Sankara's initiative, the country's name changed from "Upper Volta" to "Burkina Faso" or <i>land of the honest men</i>; (the literal translation is <i>land of the upright men</i>.)<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (March 2020)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The presidential decree was confirmed by the National Assembly on 4 August. The demonym for people of Burkina Faso, "Burkinabé", includes expatriates or descendants of people of Burkinabé origin. </p>
      <p>Sankara's government comprised the National Council for the Revolution (CNR – <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Conseil national révolutionnaire</i>), with Sankara as its president, and established popular <a href="/wiki/Committees_for_the_Defense_of_the_Revolution_(Burkina_Faso)" title="Committees for the Defense of the Revolution (Burkina Faso)">Committees for the Defense of the Revolution</a> (CDRs). The <a href="/wiki/Pioneers_of_the_Revolution" title="Pioneers of the Revolution">Pioneers of the Revolution</a> youth programme was also established. </p>
      <p>Sankara launched an ambitious socioeconomic programme for change, one of the largest ever undertaken on the African continent.<sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup> His foreign policies centred on <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialism</a>, with his government rejecting all <a href="/wiki/Foreign_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign aid">foreign aid</a>, pushing for <a href="/wiki/Odious_debt" title="Odious debt">odious debt</a> reduction, nationalising all land and mineral wealth and averting the power and influence of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>. His domestic policies included a nationwide literacy campaign, land redistribution to peasants, railway and road construction and the outlawing of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grila2_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grila2-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sankara pushed for agrarian self-sufficiency and promoted public health by vaccinating 2,500,000 children against <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grila2_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grila2-15">[15]</a></sup> His national agenda also included planting over 10,000,000 trees to halt the growing <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>. Sankara called on every village to build a medical dispensary and had over 350 communities build schools with their own labour.<sup id="cite_ref-UprightDVD_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UprightDVD-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="1987_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1987_coup_d'état">1987 coup d'état</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1987 coup d'état">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 15 October 1987, Sankara, along with twelve other officials, died in a coup d'état organized by Blaise Compaoré, Sankara's former colleague, who served as Burkina Faso's president from October 1987 until October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> After the coup and although Sankara was known to be dead, some CDRs mounted an armed resistance to the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of Burkina Faso">army</a> for several days.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A majority<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (March 2020)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> of Burkinabé citizens hold that <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Europe_and_Foreign_Affairs" title="Ministry of Europe and Foreign Affairs">France's foreign ministry</a>, the Quai d'Orsay, was behind Compaoré in organizing the coup. </p>
      <p>Compaoré gave as one of the reasons for the coup the deterioration in relations with neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Compaoré argued that Sankara had jeopardised foreign relations with the former colonial power (France) and with neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersChe2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersChe2-13">[13]</a></sup> Following the coup Compaoré immediately reversed the nationalizations, overturned nearly all of Sankara's policies, returned the country back into the IMF fold, and ultimately spurned most of Sankara's legacy. Following an alleged <a href="/wiki/1989_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1989 Burkinabé coup d'état attempt">coup-attempt in 1989</a>, Compaoré introduced limited democratic reforms in 1990. Under the new (1991) <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Constitution of Burkina Faso">constitution</a>, Compaoré was <a href="/wiki/1991_Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election" title="1991 Burkinabé presidential election">re-elected</a> without opposition in December 1991. In 1998 Compaoré won <a href="/wiki/1998_Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election" title="1998 Burkinabé presidential election">election</a> in a landslide. In 2004, 13 people were tried for plotting a coup against President Compaoré and the coup's alleged mastermind was sentenced to life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Burkina Faso remained one of the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed country">least-developed countries</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Compaoré's government played the role of negotiator in several West-African disputes, including the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Ivorian_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–11 Ivorian crisis">2010–11 Ivorian crisis</a>, the Inter-Togolese Dialogue (2007), and the <a href="/wiki/2012_Malian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Malian coup d'état">2012 Malian Crisis</a>. </p>
      <p>Between February and April 2011, the death of a schoolboy provoked <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkinab%C3%A8_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Burkinabè protests">protests</a> throughout the country, coupled with a military mutiny and a magistrates' strike. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="October_2014_protests">October 2014 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: October 2014 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_Burkinab%C3%A9_uprising" title="2014 Burkinabé uprising">2014 Burkinabé uprising</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Starting on 28 October 2014 protesters began to march and demonstrate in Ouagadougou against President Blaise Compaoré, who appeared<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (March 2020)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> ready to amend the constitution and extend his 27-year rule. On 30 October some protesters set fire to the parliament building<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and took over the national TV headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ouagadougou Airport">Ouagadougou International Airport</a> closed and MPs suspended the vote on changing the constitution (the change would have allowed Compaoré to stand for re-election in 2015). Later in the day, the military dissolved all government institutions and imposed a <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 October 2014, President Compaoré, facing mounting pressure, resigned after 27&nbsp;years in office.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yacouba_Isaac_Zida" title="Yacouba Isaac Zida">Lt. Col. Isaac Zida</a> said that he would lead the country during its transitional period before the planned <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 2015">2015 presidential election</a>, but there were concerns<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (March 2020)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> over his close ties to the former president.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In November 2014 opposition parties, <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil-society</a> groups and religious leaders adopted a plan for a transitional authority to guide Burkina Faso to elections.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Under the plan <a href="/wiki/Michel_Kafando" title="Michel Kafando">Michel Kafando</a> became the transitional <a href="/wiki/President_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Burkina Faso">President of Burkina Faso</a> and Lt. Col. Zida became the acting Prime Minister and Defense Minister. </p> 
      <h4><span id="2015_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_coup_d'état">2015 coup d'état</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2015 coup d'état">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2015 Burkinabé coup d'état">2015 Burkinabé coup d'état</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 16 September 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_of_Presidential_Security" title="Regiment of Presidential Security">Regiment of Presidential Security</a> (RSP) seized the country's president and prime minister and then declared the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_Democracy" title="National Council for Democracy">National Council for Democracy</a> the new national government.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> However, on 22 September 2015, the coup leader, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Diend%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Gilbert Diendéré">Gilbert Diendéré</a>, apologized and promised to restore civilian government.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> On 23 September 2015 the prime minister and interim president were restored to power.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="November_2015_election">November 2015 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: November 2015 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_general_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé general election, 2015">Burkinabé general election, 2015</a>
      </div> 
      <p>General elections took place in Burkina Faso on 29 November 2015. <a href="/wiki/Roch_Marc_Christian_Kabor%C3%A9" title="Roch Marc Christian Kaboré">Roch Marc Christian Kaboré</a> won the election in the first round with 53.5% of the vote, defeating businessman <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%A9phirin_Diabr%C3%A9" title="Zéphirin Diabré">Zéphirin Diabré</a>, who took 29.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-Kabore_wins_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kabore_wins-20">[20]</a></sup> Kaboré was sworn in as president on 29 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-swears_in_new_president_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swears_in_new_president-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrorist_attacks">Terrorist attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terrorist attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Ouagadougou_attacks" title="2016 Ouagadougou attacks">2016 Ouagadougou attacks</a>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Terrorism in Burkina Faso">Terrorism in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In February 2016 a terrorist attack occurred at the Splendid Hotel and Capuccino café-bar in the centre of Ouagadougou: 30 people died. <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Islamic_Maghreb" title="Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb">Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb</a> (AQIM) and <a href="/wiki/Al-Mourabitoun_(militant_group)" title="Al-Mourabitoun (militant group)">Al-Mourabitoun</a>, two groups which until then had mostly operated in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, claimed responsibility for the attack. Since then, similar groups have carried out numerous<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (March 2020)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> attacks in the northern and eastern parts of the country. One terrorist attack occurred on the evening of Friday, 11 October 2019 on a mosque in the village of Salmossi near the border with Mali, leaving 16 people dead and two injured.<sup id="cite_ref-France_24_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France_24-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Politics of Burkina Faso">Politics of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinabe_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Burkinabe coup d'état">2015 Burkinabe coup d'état</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/170px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/255px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png/340px-Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png 2x" data-file-width="605" data-file-height="653"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Blaise_Compaor%C3%A9_2014_White_House.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President Blaise Compaoré ruled Burkina Faso from a coup d'état in 1987 until he lost power in 2014.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4512" data-file-height="3384"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Assemblee_Nationale_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Burkina_Faso" title="National Assembly of Burkina Faso">National Assembly</a> building in downtown <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With French help, Blaise Compaoré seized power in a coup d'état in 1987. He overthrew his long-time friend and ally <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sankara" title="Thomas Sankara">Thomas Sankara</a>, who was killed in the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Constitution of Burkina Faso">constitution</a> of 2 June 1991 established a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential government</a>: its parliament could be dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Burkina_Faso" title="List of heads of state of Burkina Faso">President of the Republic</a>, who was to be <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Elections in Burkina Faso">elected</a> for a term of seven years. In 2000, the constitution was amended to reduce the presidential term to five years and set term limits to two, preventing successive re-election. The amendment took effect during the 2005 elections. If passed beforehand, it would have prevented Compaoré from being reelected. </p>
      <p>Other presidential candidates challenged the election results. But in October 2005, the constitutional council ruled that, because Compaoré was the sitting president in 2000, the amendment would not apply to him until the end of his second term in office. This cleared the way for his candidacy in <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso_presidential_elections,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkina Faso presidential elections, 2005">the 2005 election</a>. On 13 November 2005, Compaoré was reelected in a landslide, because of a divided political opposition. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_presidential_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé presidential election, 2010">2010 Presidential elections</a>, President Compaoré was re-elected. Only 1.6&nbsp;million Burkinabés voted, out of a total population 10&nbsp;times that size. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkinab%C3%A8_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Burkinabè protests">2011 Burkinabè protests</a> were a series of popular protests that called for the resignation of Compaoré, democratic reforms, higher wages for troops and public servants and economic freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> As a result, governors were replaced and wages for public servants were raised.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The parliament consisted of <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">one chamber</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Burkina_Faso)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly (Burkina Faso)">National Assembly</a> which had 111&nbsp;seats with members elected to serve five-year terms. There was also a constitutional chamber, composed of ten members, and an economic and social council whose roles were purely consultative. The 1991 constitution created a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament but the upper house (Chamber of Representatives) was abolished in 2002. </p>
      <p>The Compaoré administration had worked to <a href="/wiki/Decentralization#Government_decentralization" title="Decentralization">decentralize power</a> by devolving some of its powers to regions and municipal authorities. But the widespread distrust of politicians and lack of political involvement by many residents complicated this process. Critics described this as a hybrid decentralisation.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">Political freedoms</a> are severely restricted in Burkina Faso. <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">Human rights organizations</a> had criticised the Compaoré administration for numerous acts of state-sponsored violence against journalists and other politically active members of society.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In mid-September 2015 the Kafando government, along with the rest of the post-October 2014 political order, was <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinabe_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Burkinabe coup d'état">temporarily overthrown</a> in a coup attempt by the <a href="/wiki/Regiment_of_Presidential_Security" title="Regiment of Presidential Security">Regiment of Presidential Security</a> (RSP). They installed Gilbert Diendéré as chairman of the new <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_Democracy" title="National Council for Democracy">National Council for Democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DailyTelegraph_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyTelegraph-18">[18]</a></sup> On 23 September 2015, the prime minister and interim president were restored to power.<sup id="cite_ref-npr-back_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-back-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-npr-apology_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-npr-apology-72">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_general_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé general election, 2015">national elections</a> were subsequently rescheduled for 29 November. </p>
      <p>Kaboré won the election in the first round of voting, receiving 53.5% of the vote against 29.7% for the second place candidate, <a href="/wiki/Zephirin_Diabr%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Zephirin Diabré">Zephirin Diabré</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kabore_wins_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kabore_wins-20">[20]</a></sup> He was sworn in as president on 29 December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-swears_in_new_president_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swears_in_new_president-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> described the president as a "French-educated banker ... [who] sees himself as a social democrat, and has pledged to reduce youth unemployment, improve education and healthcare, and make health provision for children under six free of charge".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The prime minister is head of government and is appointed by the president with the approval of the National Assembly. He is responsible for recommending a cabinet for appointment by the president. Paul Kaba Thieba was appointed PM in early 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a World Bank Report in late 2018, the political climate was stable; the government was facing "social discontent marked by major strikes and protests, organized by unions in several economic sectors, to demand salary increases and social benefits .... and increasingly frequent jihadist attacks". The next elections would be held in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Constitution of Burkina Faso">Constitution of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2015, Kaboré promised to revise the 1991 constitution. The revision was completed in 2018. One condition prevents any individual from serving as president for more than ten years either consecutively or intermittently and provides a method for impeaching a president. A referendum on the constitution for the Fifth Republic was scheduled for 24 March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Certain rights are also enshrined in the revised wording: access to drinking water, to decent housing and a recognition of the right to civil disobedience, for example. The referendum was required because the opposition parties in Parliament refused to sanction the proposed text.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Foreign relations of Burkina Faso">Foreign relations of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/G5_Sahel" title="G5 Sahel">G5 Sahel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel%E2%80%93Saharan_States" title="Community of Sahel–Saharan States">Community of Sahel–Saharan States</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, and United Nations. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Burkina Faso">Military of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of Burkina Faso">army</a> consists of some 6,000&nbsp;men in voluntary service, augmented by a part-time national People's Militia composed of civilians between 25 and 35&nbsp;years of age who are trained in both military and civil duties. According to <i>Jane's Sentinel Country Risk Assessment</i>, Burkina Faso's Army is undermanned for its force structure and poorly equipped, but has wheeled light-armour vehicles, and may have developed useful combat expertise through interventions in Liberia and elsewhere in Africa. </p>
      <p>In terms of training and equipment, the regular Army is believed to be neglected in relation to the élite Regiment of Presidential Security (French: <i lang="fr">Régiment de la Sécurité Présidentielle</i> – RSP). Reports have emerged in recent years of disputes over pay and conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> There is an air force with some 19&nbsp;operational aircraft, but no navy, as the country is landlocked. Military expenses constitute approximately 1.2% of the nation's GDP. </p>
      <p>In April 2011, there was an <a href="/wiki/2011_Burkina_Faso_mutiny" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Burkina Faso mutiny">army mutiny</a>; the president named new chiefs of staff, and a curfew was imposed in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Law enforcement in Burkina Faso">Law enforcement in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso employs numerous police and security forces, generally modeled after organizations used by <a href="/wiki/French_police" class="mw-redirect" title="French police">French police</a>. France continues to provide significant support and training to police forces. The <i>Gendarmerie Nationale</i> is organized along military lines, with most police services delivered at the brigade level. The <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a> operates under the authority of the Minister of Defence, and its members are employed chiefly in the rural areas and along borders.<sup id="cite_ref-Das,_pp.&nbsp;139–141_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Das,_pp._139–141-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is a municipal police force controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Territorial_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Territorial Administration">Ministry of Territorial Administration</a>; a national police force controlled by the Ministry of Security; and an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Regiment_of_Presidential_Security" title="Regiment of Presidential Security">Regiment of Presidential Security</a> (<i>Régiment de la Sécurité Présidentielle</i>, or RSP), a 'palace guard' devoted to the protection of the President of the Republic. Both the gendarmerie and the national police are subdivided into both administrative and judicial police functions; the former are detailed to protect public order and provide security, the latter are charged with criminal investigations.<sup id="cite_ref-Das,_pp.&nbsp;139–141_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Das,_pp._139–141-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All foreigners and citizens are required to carry photo ID passports, or other forms of identification or risk a fine, and police spot identity checks are commonplace for persons traveling by auto, <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">bush-taxi</a>, or bus.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_sat.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/220px-Burkina_sat.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/330px-Burkina_sat.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Burkina_sat.png/440px-Burkina_sat.png 2x" data-file-width="950" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_sat.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of Burkina Faso
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Geography of Burkina Faso">Geography of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg/330px-Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg" decoding="async" width="330" height="392" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg/495px-Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg/660px-Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="979" data-file-height="1162"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_Map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Burkina Faso
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_parallel_north" title="9th parallel north">9°</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">15°N</a> (a small area is north of 15°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">6°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/3rd_meridian_east" title="3rd meridian east">3°E</a>. </p>
      <p>It is made up of two major types of countryside.
