The larger part of the country is covered by a <a href="/wiki/Peneplain" title="Peneplain">peneplain</a>, which forms a gently undulating landscape with, in some areas, a few isolated hills, the last vestiges of a <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">massif</a>. The southwest of the country, on the other hand, forms a <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> massif, where the highest peak, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9nakourou" class="mw-redirect" title="Ténakourou">Ténakourou</a>, is found at an elevation of 749 meters (2,457&nbsp;ft). The massif is bordered by sheer cliffs up to 150&nbsp;m (492&nbsp;ft) high. The average altitude of Burkina Faso is 400&nbsp;m (1,312&nbsp;ft) and the difference between the highest and lowest terrain is no greater than 600&nbsp;m (1,969&nbsp;ft). Burkina Faso is therefore a relatively flat country. </p>
      <p>The country owes its former name of Upper Volta to three rivers which cross it: the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black Volta</a> (or <i>Mouhoun</i>), the <a href="/wiki/White_Volta" title="White Volta">White Volta</a> (<i>Nakambé</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Volta" title="Red Volta">Red Volta</a> (<i>Nazinon</i>). The Black Volta is one of the country's only two rivers which flow year-round, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Komo%C3%A9_River" title="Komoé River">Komoé</a>, which flows to the southwest. The basin of the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a> also <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drains</a> 27% of the country's surface. </p>
      <p>The Niger's <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> – the Béli, Gorouol, Goudébo, and Dargol – are <a href="/wiki/Torrent_(stream)" class="mw-redirect" title="Torrent (stream)">seasonal streams</a> and flow for only four to six months a year. They still can flood and overflow, however. The country also contains numerous lakes – the principal ones are Tingrela, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Bam" title="Lake Bam">Bam</a>, and Dem. The country contains large ponds, as well, such as Oursi, Béli, Yomboli, and Markoye. <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">Water shortages</a> are often a problem, especially in the north of the country. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:WP_35,_SDr9776.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/220px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/330px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG/440px-WP_35%2C_SDr9776.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:WP_35,_SDr9776.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">Savannah</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Gbomblora_Department" title="Gbomblora Department">Gbomblora Department</a>, on the road from <a href="/wiki/Gaoua" title="Gaoua">Gaoua</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bati%C3%A9,_Burkina_Faso" title="Batié, Burkina Faso">Batié</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso lies within two terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Regions of Burkina Faso">Regions of Burkina Faso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Provinces of Burkina Faso">Provinces of Burkina Faso</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Departments of Burkina Faso">Departments of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country is divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Regions of Burkina Faso">13&nbsp;administrative regions</a>. These regions encompass <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Provinces of Burkina Faso">45&nbsp;provinces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Departments of Burkina Faso">301&nbsp;departments</a>. Each region is administered by a governor. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1351" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_BFA_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso has a primarily tropical climate with two very distinct seasons. In the rainy season, the country receives between 60 and 90&nbsp;cm (23.6 and 35.4&nbsp;in) of rainfall; in the dry season, the <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> – a hot dry wind from the Sahara – blows. The rainy season lasts approximately four months, May/June through September, and is shorter in the north of the country. Three climatic zones can be defined: the Sahel, the Sudan-Sahel, and the Sudan-Guinea. The <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> in the north typically receives less than 60&nbsp;cm (23.6&nbsp;in)<sup id="cite_ref-relationship_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relationship-84">[84]</a></sup> of rainfall per&nbsp;year and has high temperatures, 5–47&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (41–117&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>). </p>
      <p>A relatively dry <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical savanna">tropical savanna</a>, the Sahel extends beyond the borders of Burkina Faso, from the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> to the Atlantic Ocean, and borders the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> to its north and the fertile region of the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudan</a> to the south. Situated between 11°3' and 13°5'&nbsp;north <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>, the Sudan-Sahel region is a transitional zone with regards to rainfall and temperature. Further to the south, the Sudan-Guinea zone receives more than 90&nbsp;cm (35.4&nbsp;in)<sup id="cite_ref-relationship_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relationship-84">[84]</a></sup> of rain each year and has cooler average temperatures. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Burkina Faso's natural resources include gold, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pumice" title="Pumice">pumice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salt_mining" title="Salt mining">salt</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_and_the_environment">Wildlife and the environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Wildlife and the environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Wildlife of Burkina Faso">Wildlife of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso has a larger number of elephants than many countries in West Africa. Lions, leopards and buffalo can also be found here, including the dwarf or red buffalo, a smaller reddish-brown animal which looks like a fierce kind of short-legged cow. Other large predators live in Burkina Faso, such as the cheetah, the caracal or African lynx, the spotted hyena and the African wild dog, one of the continent's most endangered species.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burkina Faso's <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_in_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildlife in Burkina Faso">fauna and flora</a> are protected in four national parks: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The W National Park in the east which passes Burkina Faso, Benin, and Niger</li> 
       <li>The Arly Wildlife Reserve (Arly National Park in the east)</li> 
       <li>The Léraba-Comoé Classified Forest and Partial Reserve of Wildlife in the west</li> 
       <li>The Mare aux Hippopotames in the west</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>and several reserves: see <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Africa" title="List of national parks in Africa">List of national parks in Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserves_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature reserves of Burkina Faso">Nature reserves of Burkina Faso</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Economy of Burkina Faso">Economy of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Burkina_Faso.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Burkina Faso's exports in 2009. Every year gold and cotton constitute more than 70% of the country's exports and the prices of these commodities have fluctuated significantly in the past 10 years. See the 2016 figure
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The value of Burkina Faso's exports fell from $2.77&nbsp;billion in 2011 to $754&nbsp;million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Agriculture represents 32% of its gross domestic product and occupies 80% of the working population. It consists mostly of rearing livestock. Especially in the south and southwest, the people grow crops of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_millet" title="Pearl millet">pearl millet</a>, maize (corn), peanuts, rice and cotton, with surpluses to be sold. A large part of the economic activity of the country is funded by international aid, despite having gold ores in abundance. </p>
      <p>The top five export commodities in 2017 were as follows, in order of importance: gems and precious metals, US$1.9&nbsp;billion (78.5% of total exports), cotton, $198.7&nbsp;million (8.3%), ores, slag, ash, $137.6&nbsp;million (5.8%), fruits, nuts: $76.6&nbsp;million (3.2%) and oil seeds: $59.5&nbsp;million (2.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A December 2018 report from the World Bank indicates that in 2017, economic growth increased to 6.4% in 2017 (vs. 5.9% in 2016) primarily due to gold production and increased investment in infrastructure. The increase in consumption linked to growth of the wage bill also supported economic growth. Inflation remained low, 0.4% that year but the public deficit grew to 7.7% of GDP (vs. 3.5% in 2016). The government was continuing to get financial aid and loans to finance the debt. To finance the public deficit, the Government combined concessional aid and borrowing on the regional market. The World Bank said that the economic outlook remained favorable in the short and medium term, although that could be negatively impacted. Risks included high oil prices (imports), lower prices of gold and cotton (exports) as well as terrorist threat and labour strikes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burkina Faso is part of the <a href="/wiki/West_African_Monetary_and_Economic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="West African Monetary and Economic Union">West African Monetary and Economic Union</a> (UMEOA) and has adopted the <a href="/wiki/West_African_CFA_franc" title="West African CFA franc">CFA franc</a>. This is issued by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_West_African_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Bank of the West African States">Central Bank of the West African States</a> (BCEAO), situated in <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>, Senegal. The BCEAO manages the monetary and reserve policy of the member states, and provides regulation and oversight of financial sector and banking activity. A legal framework regarding licensing, bank activities, organizational and capital requirements, inspections and sanctions (all applicable to all countries of the Union) is in place, having been reformed significantly in 1999. <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">Microfinance</a> institutions are governed by a separate law, which regulates microfinance activities in all WAEMU countries. The insurance sector is regulated through the Inter-African Conference on Insurance Markets (CIMA).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Essakane_Mill_in_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Processing facilities at the Essakane Mine in Burkina Faso
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2018, tourism was almost non-existent in large parts of the country. The U.S. government (and others) warn their citizens not to travel into large parts of Burkina Faso: "The northern Sahel border region shared with Mali and Niger due to crime and terrorism. The provinces of Kmoandjari, Tapoa, Kompienga, and Gourma in East Region due to crime and terrorism".<sup id="cite_ref-auto_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2018 CIA World Factbook provides this updated summary. "Burkina Faso is a poor, landlocked country that depends on adequate rainfall. Irregular patterns of rainfall, poor soil, and the lack of adequate communications and other infrastructure contribute to the economy's vulnerability to external shocks. About 80% of the population is engaged in subsistence farming and cotton is the main cash crop. The country has few natural resources and a weak industrial base. Cotton and gold are Burkina Faso's key exports ...The country has seen an upswing in gold exploration, production, and exports. </p>
      <p>While the end of the political crisis has allowed Burkina Faso's economy to resume positive growth, the country's fragile security situation could put these gains at risk. Political insecurity in neighboring Mali, unreliable energy supplies, and poor transportation links pose long-term challenges." The report also highlights the 2018–2020 International Monetary Fund program, including the government's plan to "reduce the budget deficit and preserve critical spending on social services and priority public investments".<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A 2018 report by the African Development Bank Group discussed a macroeconomic evolution: "higher investment and continued spending on social services and security that will add to the budget deficit". This group's prediction for 2018 indicated that the budget deficit would be reduced to 4.8% of GDP in 2018 and to 2.9% in 2019. Public debt associated with the National Economic and Social Development Plan was estimated at 36.9% of GDP in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burkina Faso is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The country also belongs to the United Nations, International Monetary Fund, World Bank, and World Trade Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining in Burkina Faso">Mining in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There is mining of copper, iron, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, gold, <a href="/wiki/Cassiterite" title="Cassiterite">cassiterite</a> (tin ore), and phosphates.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> These operations provide employment and generate international aid. Gold production increased 32% in 2011 at six gold mine sites, making Burkina Faso the fourth-largest gold producer in Africa, after South Africa, Mali and Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A 2018 report indicated that the country expected record 55 tonnes of gold in that year, a two-thirds increase over 2013. According to Oumarou Idani, there is a more important issue. "We have to diversify production. We mostly only produce gold, but we have huge potential in manganese, zinc, lead, copper, nickel and limestone".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_insecurity">Food insecurity <span class="anchor" id="Food_insecurity_in_Burkina_Faso"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Food insecurity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a>, a multidimensional tool used to measure and track a country's hunger levels,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Burkina Faso ranked 65 out of 78&nbsp;countries in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Know_About_Hunger_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know_About_Hunger-97">[97]</a></sup> It is estimated that there are currently over 1.5&nbsp;million children who are at risk of food insecurity in Burkina Faso, with around 350,000&nbsp;children who are in need of emergency medical assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Know_About_Hunger_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know_About_Hunger-97">[97]</a></sup> However, only about a third of these children will actually receive adequate medical attention.<sup id="cite_ref-Cost_of_Hunger_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cost_of_Hunger-98">[98]</a></sup> Only 11.4&nbsp;percent of children under the age of two receive the daily recommended number of meals.<sup id="cite_ref-Know_About_Hunger_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know_About_Hunger-97">[97]</a></sup> Stunted growth as a result of food insecurity is a severe problem in Burkina Faso, affecting at least a third of the population from 2008 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Additionally, stunted children, on average, tend to complete less school than children with normal growth development,<sup id="cite_ref-Cost_of_Hunger_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cost_of_Hunger-98">[98]</a></sup> further contributing to the low levels of education of the Burkina Faso population.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> expects that approximately 500,000&nbsp;children under age&nbsp;5 in Burkina Faso will suffer from acute malnutrition in 2015, including around 149,000 who will suffer from its most life-threatening form.<sup id="cite_ref-ECHO_Factsheet_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECHO_Factsheet-101">[101]</a></sup> Rates of micronutrient deficiencies are also high.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_Program_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_Program-102">[102]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Survey</a> (DHS&nbsp;2010), 49&nbsp;percent of women and 88&nbsp;percent of children under the age of five suffer from anemia.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_Program_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_Program-102">[102]</a></sup> Forty percent of infant deaths can be attributed to malnutrition, and in turn, these infant mortality rates have decreased Burkina Faso's total work force by 13.6&nbsp;percent, demonstrating how food security affects more aspects of life beyond health.<sup id="cite_ref-Know_About_Hunger_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Know_About_Hunger-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>These high rates of food insecurity and the accompanying effects are even more prevalent in rural populations compared to urban ones, as access to health services in rural areas is much more limited and awareness and education of children's nutritional needs is lower.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An October 2018 report by <a href="/wiki/USAid" class="mw-redirect" title="USAid">USAid</a> stated that droughts and floods remained problematic, and that "violence and insecurity are disrupting markets, trade and livelihoods activities in some of Burkina Faso's northern and eastern areas". The report estimated that over 954,300 people needed food security support, and that, according to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, an "estimated 187,200 children under 5 years of age will experience severe acute malnutrition". Agencies providing assistance at the time included USAID's Office of Food for Peace (FFP) working with the UN <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, the NGO <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> Intermón and <a href="/wiki/ACDI/VOCA" title="ACDI/VOCA">ACDI/VOCA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Approaches_to_improving_food_security">Approaches to improving food security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Approaches to improving food security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Food_Programme">World Food Programme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: World Food Programme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The United Nations’ World Food Programme has worked on programs that are geared towards increasing food security in Burkina Faso. The Protracted Relief and Recovery Operation&nbsp;200509 (PRRO) was formed to respond to the high levels of malnutrition in Burkina Faso, following the food and nutrition crisis in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> The efforts of this project are mostly geared towards the treatment and prevention of malnutrition and include take home rations for the caretakers of those children who are being treated for malnutrition.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> Additionally, the activities of this operation contribute to families' abilities to withstand future food crises. Better nutrition among the two most vulnerable groups, young children and pregnant women, prepares them to be able to respond better in times when food security is compromised, such as in droughts.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Country Programme (CP) has two parts: food and nutritional assistance to people with HIV/AIDS, and a school feeding program for all primary schools in the Sahel region.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-106">[106]</a></sup> The HIV/AIDS nutrition program aims to better the nutritional recovery of those who are living with HIV/AIDS and to protect at-risk children and orphans from malnutrition and food security.<sup id="cite_ref-Brief_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brief-106">[106]</a></sup> As part of the school feeding component, the Country Programme's goals are to increase enrollment and attendance in schools in the Sahel region, where enrollment rates are below the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> Furthermore, the program aims at improving gender parity rates in these schools, by providing girls with high attendance in the last two years of primary school with take-home rations of cereals as an incentive to households, encouraging them to send their girls to school.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The WFP concluded the formation of a subsequently approved plan in August 2018 "to support the Government's vision of 'a democratic, unified and united nation, transforming the structure of its economy and achieving a strong and inclusive growth through patterns of sustainable consumption and production.' It will take important steps in WFP's new strategic direction for strengthened national and local capacities to enable the Government and communities to own, manage, and implement food and nutrition security programmes by 2030".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Bank">World Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: World Bank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a> was established in 1944, and comprises five institutions whose shared goals are to end extreme poverty by 2030 and to promote shared prosperity by fostering income growth of the lower forty percent of every country.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> One of the main projects the World Bank is working on to reduce food insecurity in Burkina Faso is the Agricultural Productivity and Food Security Project.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> According to the World Bank, the objective of this project is to "improve the capacity of poor producers to increase food production and to ensure improved availability of food products in rural markets."<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> The Agricultural Productivity and Food Security Project has three main parts. Its first component is to work towards the improvement of food production, including financing grants and providing 'voucher for work' programs for households who cannot pay their contribution in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> The project's next component involves improving the ability of food products, particularly in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> This includes supporting the marketing of food products, and aims to strengthen the capabilities of stakeholders to control the variability of food products and supplies at local and national levels.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> Lastly, the third component of this project focuses on institutional development and capacity building. Its goal is to reinforce the capacities of service providers and institutions who are specifically involved in project implementation.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> The project's activities aim to build capacities of service providers, strengthen the capacity of food producer organizations, strengthen agricultural input supply delivery methods, and manage and evaluate project activities.<sup id="cite_ref-AgProdFSP_109-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AgProdFSP-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The December 2018 report by the World Bank indicated that the poverty rate fell slightly between 2009 and 2014, from 46% to a still high 40.1%. The report provided this updated summary of the country's development challenges: "Burkina Faso remains vulnerable to climatic shocks related to changes in rainfall patterns and to fluctuations in the prices of its export commodities on world markets. Its economic and social development will, to some extent, be contingent on political stability in the country and the subregion, its openness to international trade, and export diversification".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_security">Food security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Food security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg/220px-Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg/330px-Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg/440px-Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_-_Tarfila_Farming_Group.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A group of farmers in Tarfila, Burkina Faso
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso is faced with high levels of <a href="/wiki/Food_insecurity" class="mw-redirect" title="Food insecurity">food insecurity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> As defined by the 1996 <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Summit" title="World Food Summit">World Food Summit</a>, "food security exists when all people, at all times, have physical and economic access to sufficient safe and nutritious food that meets their dietary needs and food preferences for an active and healthy lifestyle."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> There has not been much successful improvement on this issue of food security within recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> Burkina Faso's rapidly growing population (around 3.6% annually) continues to put a strain on the country's resources and infrastructure, which can further limit accessibility to food.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because the country is landlocked and prone to <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disasters</a>, including drought and floods, many families struggle to protect themselves from severe <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> While recent harvest productions have improved some, much of the population is still having a hard time overcoming the continuous food and nutrition crises of the past decade.<sup id="cite_ref-ECHO_Factsheet_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECHO_Factsheet-101">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</a> is especially common in women and children, with large amounts of the population suffering from <a href="/wiki/Stunted_growth" title="Stunted growth">stunted growth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Micronutrient_deficiencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Micronutrient deficiencies">micronutrient deficiencies</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Food insecurity has grown to be a structural problem in Burkina Faso, only to be intensified by high <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a>. All of these factors combined with high poverty levels have left Burkina Faso vulnerable to chronic high levels of food insecurity and malnutrition.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_economic_causes">Social and economic causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Social and economic causes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Poverty continues to be strongly linked to food insecurity.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> As one of the poorest countries in the world, Burkina Faso has around 43.7% of its population living under the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty Line">Poverty Line</a><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and ranked 185 out of 188&nbsp;countries on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a> Human Development Index in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Food_Programme_105-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Food_Programme-105">[105]</a></sup> The Human Development Index is a measure of quality of life, taking into account three main areas of human development: longevity, education, and economic standard of living.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> These high levels of poverty found in Burkina Faso, combined with the soaring food prices of the <a href="/wiki/Global_food_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Global food crisis">global food crisis</a> continue to contribute to Burkina Faso's issue of food insecurity.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The global food crisis of 2007–2008 was a drastic surge in food prices that led to high rates of hunger, malnutrition, and political and economic instability in nations across the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> This strongly affected Burkina Faso because around 80% of Burkina Faso's population is rural, relying on <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence farming">subsistence farming</a> to make a living.<sup id="cite_ref-ECHO_Factsheet_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECHO_Factsheet-101">[101]</a></sup> For instance, when natural disasters such as floods, droughts, or locust attacks occur and cause crops to fail, farmers in Burkina Faso become dependent on grain purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_Thor_West_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_Thor_West-119">[119]</a></sup> Because of the global food crisis, local grain prices dramatically increased, limiting farmers' access to grain through market exchanges.<sup id="cite_ref-Colin_Thor_West_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colin_Thor_West-119">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_services">Infrastructure and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Infrastructure and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/220px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/330px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg/440px-Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3556" data-file-height="2667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_march%C3%A9_de_Koudougou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <i>Grand marché</i> in <a href="/wiki/Koudougou" title="Koudougou">Koudougou</a>, Burkina Faso
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>While <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">services</a> remain underdeveloped, the National Office for Water and Sanitation (ONEA), a <a href="/wiki/State-owned" class="mw-redirect" title="State-owned">state-owned</a> <a href="/wiki/Utility_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Utility company">utility company</a> run along commercial lines, is emerging as one of the best-performing utility companies in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-120">[120]</a></sup> High levels of autonomy and a skilled and dedicated management have driven ONEA's ability to improve production of and access to clean water.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2000, nearly 2&nbsp;million more people have access to water in the four principal urban centres in the country; the company has kept the quality of <a href="/wiki/Water_infrastructure" class="mw-redirect" title="Water infrastructure">infrastructure</a> high (less than 18% of the water is lost through leaks – one of the lowest in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>), improved financial reporting, and increased its annual revenue by an average of 12% (well above inflation).<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-120">[120]</a></sup> Challenges remain, including difficulties among some customers in paying for services, with the need to rely on international aid to expand its infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-120">[120]</a></sup> The state-owned, commercially run venture has helped the nation reach its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Development Goal">Millennium Development Goal</a> (MDG) targets in water-related areas, and has grown as a viable company.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_120-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, access to drinking water has improved over the last 28 years. According to UNICEF, access to drinking water has increased from 39 to 76% in rural areas between 1990 and 2015. In this same time span, access to drinking water increased from 75 to 97% in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">Electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A 33-megawatt solar power plant in Zagtouli, near Ouagadougou, came online in late November 2017. At the time of its construction, it was the largest solar power facility in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The growth rate in Burkina Faso is high although it continues to be plagued by corruption and incursions from terrorist groups from Mali and Niger.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/220px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/330px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg/440px-Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sudanese_Style_Railway_Station_Bobo_Dioulasso_Burkina_Faso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The railway station in <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect" title="Bobo Dioulasso">Bobo Dioulasso</a> was built during the colonial era and remains in operation.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Transport in Burkina Faso">Transport in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Transport in Burkina Faso is limited by relatively underdeveloped infrastructure. </p>
      <p>As of June 2014 the main international airport, <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ouagadougou Airport">Ouagadougou Airport</a>, had regularly scheduled flights to many destinations in West Africa as well as Paris, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. The other international airport, <a href="/wiki/Bobo_Dioulasso_Airport" title="Bobo Dioulasso Airport">Bobo Dioulasso Airport</a>, has flights to Ouagadougou and <a href="/wiki/Port_Bouet_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Bouet Airport">Abidjan</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Rail transport in Burkina Faso">Rail transport in Burkina Faso</a> consists of a single line which runs from <a href="/wiki/Kaya,_Burkina_Faso" title="Kaya, Burkina Faso">Kaya</a> to <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a> in Ivory Coast via <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koudougou" title="Koudougou">Koudougou</a>, Bobo Dioulasso and <a href="/wiki/Banfora" title="Banfora">Banfora</a>. <i>Sitarail</i> operates a passenger train three times a week along the route.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 15,000&nbsp;kilometres of roads in Burkina Faso, of which 2,500&nbsp;kilometres are paved.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Science and technology in Burkina Faso">Science and technology in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2009, Burkina Faso spent 0.20% of GDP on research and development (R&amp;D), one of the lowest ratios in West Africa. There were 48 researchers (in full-time equivalents) per million inhabitants in 2010, which is more than twice the average for sub-Saharan Africa (20 per million population in 2013) and higher than the ratio for Ghana and Nigeria (39). It is, however, much lower than the ratio for Senegal (361 per million inhabitants). In Burkina Faso in 2010, 46% of researchers were working in the health sector, 16% in engineering, 13% in natural sciences, 9% in agricultural sciences, 7% in the humanities and 4% in social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_Science_Report_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_Science_Report-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2011, the government created the Ministry of Scientific Research and Innovation. Up until then, management of science, technology and innovation had fallen under the Department of Secondary and Higher Education and Scientific Research. Within this ministry, the Directorate General for Research and Sector Statistics is responsible for planning. A separate body, the Directorate General of Scientific Research, Technology and Innovation, co-ordinates research. This is a departure from the pattern in many other West African countries where a single body fulfils both functions. The move signals the government's intention to make science and technology a development priority.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_Science_Report_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_Science_Report-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, Burkina Faso adopted a <i>National Policy for Scientific and Technical Research</i>, the strategic objectives of which are to develop R&amp;D and the application and commercialization of research results. The policy also makes provisions for strengthening the ministry's strategic and operational capacities. One of the key priorities is to improve food security and self-sufficiency by boosting capacity in agricultural and environmental sciences. The creation of a centre of excellence in 2014 at the International Institute of Water and Environmental Engineering in Ouagadougou within the World Bank project provides essential funding for capacity-building in these priority areas.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_Science_Report_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_Science_Report-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A dual priority is to promote innovative, effective and accessible health systems. The government wishes to develop, in parallel, applied sciences and technology and social and human sciences. To complement the national research policy, the government has prepared a <i>National Strategy to Popularize Technologies, Inventions and Innovations</i> (2012) and a <i>National Innovation Strategy</i> (2014). Other policies also incorporate science and technology, such as that on <i>Secondary and Higher Education and Scientific Research</i> (2010), the <i>National Policy on Food and Nutrition Security</i> (2014) and the <i>National Programme for the Rural Sector</i> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_Science_Report_126-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_Science_Report-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, Burkina Faso passed the Science, Technology and Innovation Act establishing three mechanisms for financing research and innovation, a clear indication of high-level commitment. These mechanisms are the National Fund for Education and Research, the National Fund for Research and Innovation for Development and the Forum of Scientific Research and Technological Innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_Science_Report_126-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO_Science_Report-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ouagadougou_(3839513403).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/170px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/255px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg/340px-Ouagadougou_%283839513403%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ouagadougou_(3839513403).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Burkinabè <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> man in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Demographics of Burkina Faso">Demographics of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-128">[128]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">4.3 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">11.6 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">19.8 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Burkina Faso is an ethnically integrated, secular state where most people are concentrated in the south and centre, where their density sometimes exceeds 48&nbsp;persons per square kilometre (125/sq.&nbsp;mi.). Hundreds of thousands of Burkinabè migrate regularly to Ivory Coast and Ghana, mainly for seasonal agricultural work. These flows of workers are affected by external events; the September 2002 coup attempt in Ivory Coast and the ensuing fighting meant that hundreds of thousands of Burkinabè returned to Burkina Faso. The regional economy suffered when they were unable to work.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015, most of the population belonged to "one of two West African ethnic cultural groups: the Voltaic and the Mande. Voltaic Mossi make up about 50% of the population and are descended from warriors who moved to the area from Ghana around 1100, establishing an empire that lasted over 800 years".<sup id="cite_ref-worldpopulationreview.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldpopulationreview.com-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Burkina Faso is 5.93&nbsp;children born per woman (2014 estimates), the sixth highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009 the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a>'s <i>Trafficking in Persons Report</i> reported that <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_modern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavery in modern Africa">slavery</a> in Burkina Faso continued to exist and that Burkinabè children were often the victims.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Slavery in the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> states in general, is an entrenched institution with a long history that dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_slave_trade" title="Trans-Saharan slave trade">trans-Saharan slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> In 2018, an estimated 82,000 people in the country were living under "modern slavery" according to the Global Slavery Index.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image" title="Ouagadougou"><img alt="Ouagadougou" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg/120px-LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg/180px-LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg/240px-LAICO_QUAGA_2000_HOTEL.2_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg" class="image" title="Bobo-Dioulasso"><img alt="Bobo-Dioulasso" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg/120px-Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg/180px-Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg/240px-Bobo-Dioulasso_Mosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Bobo-Dioulasso" title="Bobo-Dioulasso">Bobo-Dioulasso</a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">1</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a></td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Ethnic groups in Burkina Faso">Ethnic groups in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso's 17.3&nbsp;million people belong to two major West African ethnic cultural groups—the <a href="/wiki/Gur_languages" title="Gur languages">Voltaic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9_peoples" title="Mandé peoples">Mande</a> (whose common language is <a href="/wiki/Dioula_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioula language">Dioula</a>). The Voltaic <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Mossi</a> make up about one-half of the population. The Mossi claim descent from warriors who migrated to present-day Burkina Faso from northern Ghana around 1100&nbsp;AD. They established an empire that lasted more than 800&nbsp;years. Predominantly farmers, the Mossi kingdom is led by the <i><a href="/wiki/Mogho_Naba" class="mw-redirect" title="Mogho Naba">Mogho Naba</a>,</i> whose court is in Ouagadougou.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-129">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Languages of Burkina Faso">Languages of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Burkina Faso is a <a href="/wiki/Multilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Multilingual">multilingual</a> country. The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> is French, which was introduced during the colonial period. French is the principal language of administrative, political and judicial institutions, public services, and the press. It is the only language for laws, administration and courts. Altogether, an estimated 69&nbsp;languages are spoken in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> of which about 60&nbsp;languages are <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_language" title="Indigenous language">indigenous</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mossi_language" title="Mossi language">Mossi language</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mossi_language" title="Mossi language">Mossi</a>: <i lang="mos">Mòoré</i>) is the most spoken language in Burkina Faso, spoken by about half the population, mainly in the central region around the capital, Ouagadougou, along with other, closely related <a href="/wiki/Gurunsi_languages" title="Gurunsi languages">Gurunsi languages</a> scattered throughout Burkina. </p>
      <p>According to the 2006 Census, the languages spoken natively in Burkina Faso were <a href="/wiki/Mossi_language" title="Mossi language">Mossi</a> by 50.5% of the population, <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a> by 9.3%, <a href="/wiki/Gourmanch%C3%A9_language" title="Gourmanché language">Gourmanché</a> by 6.1%, <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a> by 4.9%, <a href="/wiki/Bissa_language" title="Bissa language">Bissa</a> by 3.2%, <a href="/wiki/Bwamu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bwamu language">Bwamu</a> by 2.1%, <a href="/wiki/Dagara_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dagara language">Dagara</a> by 2%, <a href="/wiki/San_language" class="mw-redirect" title="San language">San</a> by 1.9%, <a href="/wiki/Lobiri_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lobiri language">Lobiri</a> with 1.8%, <a href="/wiki/Ly%C3%A9l%C3%A9_language" title="Lyélé language">Lyélé</a> with 1.7%, <a href="/wiki/Bobo_language" title="Bobo language">Bobo</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9noufo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sénoufo language">Sénoufo</a> with 1.4% each, <a href="/wiki/Nuni_language" title="Nuni language">Nuni</a> by 1.2%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dafing_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dafing language (page does not exist)">Dafing</a> by 1.1%, <a href="/wiki/Tamasheq_language" title="Tamasheq language">Tamasheq</a> by 1%, <a href="/wiki/Kass%C3%A9na_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kasséna language">Kasséna</a> by 0.7%, <a href="/wiki/Gouin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Gouin language">Gouin</a> by 0.4%, <a href="/wiki/Dogon_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogon language">Dogon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songhai_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Songhai language">Songhai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gourounsi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Gourounsi language">Gourounsi</a> by 0.3% each, <a href="/wiki/Ko_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ko language">Ko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koussass%C3%A9_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Koussassé language">Koussassé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sembla_language" title="Sembla language">Sembla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Siamou_language" title="Siamou language">Siamou</a> by 0.1% each, other national languages by 5%, other African languages by 0.2%, French (the official language) by 1.3%, and other foreign languages by 0.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the west, <a href="/wiki/Mande_languages" title="Mande languages">Mande languages</a> are widely spoken, the most predominant being <a href="/wiki/Dioula_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioula language">Dioula</a> (also known as Jula or Dyula), others including <a href="/wiki/Bobo_language" title="Bobo language">Bobo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samo_language_(Burkina)" title="Samo language (Burkina)">Samo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marka_language" title="Marka language">Marka</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a> is widespread, particularly in the north. <a href="/wiki/Gourmanch%C3%A9_language" title="Gourmanché language">Gourmanché</a> is spoken in the east, while <a href="/wiki/Bissa_language" title="Bissa language">Bissa</a> is spoken in the south. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Gray"></div>

         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:GreenYellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:GreenYellow"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 60.848773868076px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
