         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Burkina Faso (2006)<sup id="cite_ref-RGPH2006a_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGPH2006a-3">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (60.5%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Christianity (23.2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:GreenYellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">Indigenous beliefs</a> (15.3%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Gray; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">Irreligious</a> and others (1.0%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg/220px-Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg/330px-Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg/440px-Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3354" data-file-height="2236"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moschee_von_Bobo-Dioulasso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Grand Mosque of <a href="/wiki/Bobo-Dioulasso" title="Bobo-Dioulasso">Bobo-Dioulasso</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Religion in Burkina Faso">Religion in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Statistics on religion in Burkina Faso can be misleading because <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and Christianity are often practiced in tandem with indigenous religious beliefs. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Burkina Faso">government of Burkina Faso</a>'s 2006 census reported that 60.5% of the population practice Islam, and that the majority of this group belong to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> branch,<sup id="cite_ref-RGPH2006_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGPH2006-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-report2010_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2010-138">[138]</a></sup> while a small minority adheres to <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A significant number of Sunni Muslims identify with the <a href="/wiki/Tijaniyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Tijaniyah">Tijaniyah</a> <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> order. The government estimated that 23.2% of the population are Christians (19% being Roman Catholics and 4.2% members of Protestant denominations); 15.3% follow <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">traditional indigenous beliefs</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Dogon_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogon religion">Dogon religion</a>, 0.6% have other religions, and 0.4% have none.<sup id="cite_ref-RGPH2006_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGPH2006-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-report2010_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2010-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Health in Burkina Faso">Health in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2016, the average life expectancy was estimated at 60 for males and 61 for females. In 2018, the under-five mortality rate and the infant mortality rate was 76&nbsp;per&nbsp;1000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2014, the median age of its inhabitants was 17 and the estimated population growth rate was 3.05%.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, health expenditures was 6.5% of GDP; the maternal mortality ratio was estimated at 300&nbsp;deaths per&nbsp;100000 live births and the physician density at 0.05&nbsp;per&nbsp;1000 population in 2010. In 2012, it was estimated that the adult HIV <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> rate (ages&nbsp;15–49) was 1.0%.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> According to the 2011 UNAIDS Report, HIV prevalence is declining among pregnant women who attend antenatal clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> According to a 2005&nbsp;World Health Organization report, an estimated 72.5% of Burkina Faso's girls and women have had <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, administered according to traditional rituals.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Central government spending on health was 3% in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, studies estimated there were as few as 10&nbsp;physicians per 100,000&nbsp;people.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-145">[145]</a></sup> In addition, there were 41&nbsp;nurses and 13&nbsp;midwives per 100,000&nbsp;people.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-145">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> has completed three surveys in Burkina Faso since 1993, and had another in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Burkina_Surveys_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkina_Surveys-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">Dengue fever</a> outbreak in 2016 killed 20 patients. Cases of the disease were reported from all 12 districts of Ouagadougou.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Education in Burkina Faso">Education in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG/220px-Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG/330px-Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG/440px-Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2692" data-file-height="1795"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gando-School-Burkina-Faso.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Gando,_Burkina_Faso" title="Gando, Burkina Faso">Gando</a> primary school. Its architect, <a href="/wiki/Di%C3%A9b%C3%A9do_Francis_K%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Diébédo Francis Kéré">Diébédo Francis Kéré</a>, received the <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_Award_for_Architecture" title="Aga Khan Award for Architecture">Aga Khan Award for Architecture</a> in 2004.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Burkina Faso is divided into primary, secondary and higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> High school costs approximately CFA&nbsp;25,000 (US$50) per year, which is far above the means of most Burkinabè families. Boys receive preference in schooling; as such, girls' education and literacy rates are far lower than their male counterparts. An increase in girls' schooling has been observed because of the government's policy of making school cheaper for girls and granting them more scholarships. </p>
      <p>To proceed from primary to middle school, middle to high school or high school to college, national exams must be passed. Institutions of higher education include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ouagadougou" title="University of Ouagadougou">University of Ouagadougou</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Polytechnic_University_of_Bobo-Dioulasso" class="mw-redirect" title="The Polytechnic University of Bobo-Dioulasso">The Polytechnic University of Bobo-Dioulasso</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Koudougou" title="University of Koudougou">University of Koudougou</a>, which is also a teacher training institution. There are some small private colleges in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a> but these are affordable to only a small portion of the population. </p>
      <p>There is also the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Ouagadougou" title="International School of Ouagadougou">International School of Ouagadougou</a> (ISO), an American-based private school located in Ouagadougou. </p>
      <p>The 2008&nbsp;UN Development Program Report ranked Burkina Faso as the country with the lowest level of literacy in the world, despite a concerted effort to double its literacy rate from 12.8% in 1990 to 25.3% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Culture of Burkina Faso">Culture of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_Nunuma_of_Winiama_maskerdanser_TMnr_20031569.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A masked Winiama dancer, ca. 1970
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Literature_in_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature in Burkina Faso">Literature in Burkina Faso</a> is based on the <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral tradition</a>, which remains important. In 1934, during French occupation, Dim-Dolobsom Ouedraogo published his <i>Maximes, pensées et devinettes mossi</i> (<i>Maximes, Thoughts and Riddles of the Mossi</i>), a record of the oral history of the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Mossi people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KS_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KS-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The oral tradition continued to have an influence on Burkinabè writers in the post-independence Burkina Faso of the 1960s, such as <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Boni" title="Nazi Boni">Nazi Boni</a> and Roger Nikiema.<sup id="cite_ref-TJA_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TJA-151">[151]</a></sup> The 1960s saw a growth in the number of playwrights being published.<sup id="cite_ref-KS_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KS-150">[150]</a></sup> Since the 1970s, literature has developed in Burkina Faso with many more writers being published.<sup id="cite_ref-JM_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Theatre of Burkina Faso">theatre of Burkina Faso</a> combines traditional Burkinabè performance with the colonial influences and post-colonial efforts to educate rural people to produce a distinctive national theatre. Traditional ritual ceremonies of the many ethnic groups in Burkina Faso have long involved dancing with <a href="/wiki/Mask" title="Mask">masks</a>. Western-style theatre became common during colonial times, heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/French_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="French theatre">French theatre</a>. With independence came a new style of theatre inspired by <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_the_Oppressed" title="Theatre of the Oppressed">forum theatre</a> aimed at educating and entertaining Burkina Faso's rural people. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_crafts">Arts and crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Arts and crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Art of Burkina Faso">Art of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg/220px-Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg/330px-Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg/440px-Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1630" data-file-height="1086"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_faso_artisan_painted_gourds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Artisan garland of decorative painted <a href="/wiki/Gourd" title="Gourd">gourds</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In addition to several rich traditional artistic heritages among the peoples, there is a large artist community in Burkina Faso, especially in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>. Much of the crafts produced are for the country's growing tourist industry. </p>
      <p>Burkina Faso also hosts the International Art and Craft Fair, Ouagadougou. It is better known by its French name as <a href="/wiki/SIAO" class="mw-redirect" title="SIAO">SIAO</a>, <i>Le Salon International de l' Artisanat de Ouagadougou</i>, and is one of the most important African handicraft fairs. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burkinab%C3%A9_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkinabé cuisine">Burkinabé cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fufu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Fufu.jpg/220px-Fufu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Fufu.jpg/330px-Fufu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Fufu.jpg/440px-Fufu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fufu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A plate of <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a> (right) accompanied with <a href="/wiki/Peanut_soup" title="Peanut soup">peanut soup</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Typical of West African cuisine, Burkina Faso's cuisine is based on <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple foods</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, rice, maize, peanuts, potatoes, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ox_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ox-153">[153]</a></sup> The most common sources of animal protein are chicken, chicken eggs and fresh water fish. A typical Burkinabè beverage is Banji or Palm Wine, which is fermented <a href="/wiki/Palm_wine" title="Palm wine">palm sap</a>; and Zoom-kom, or "grain water" purportedly the national drink of Burkina Faso. Zoom-kom is milky-looking and whitish, having a water and cereal base, best drunk with ice cubes. In the more rural regions, in the outskirts of Burkina, you would find Dolo, which is drink made from fermented millet.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Cinema of Burkina Faso">Cinema of Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Burkina_Faso" title="Cinema of Burkina Faso">cinema of Burkina Faso</a> is an important part of West African and African film industry.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Burkina's contribution to <a href="/wiki/African_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="African cinema">African cinema</a> started with the establishment of the film festival <a href="/wiki/FESPACO" class="mw-redirect" title="FESPACO">FESPACO</a> (Festival Panafricain du Cinéma et de la Télévision de Ouagadougou), which was launched as a film week in 1969. Many of the nation's filmmakers are known internationally and have won international prizes. </p>
      <p>For many years the headquarters of the Federation of Panafrican Filmmakers (FEPACI) was in Ouagadougou, rescued in 1983 from a period of moribund inactivity by the enthusiastic support and funding of President Sankara. (In 2006 the Secretariat of FEPACI moved to South Africa, but the headquarters of the organization is still in Ouagadougou.) Among the best known directors from Burkina Faso are <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Kabor%C3%A9" title="Gaston Kaboré">Gaston Kaboré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idrissa_Ouedraogo" class="mw-redirect" title="Idrissa Ouedraogo">Idrissa Ouedraogo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dani_Kouyate" class="mw-redirect" title="Dani Kouyate">Dani Kouyate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Burkina produces popular television series such as <i>Les Bobodiouf</i>. Internationally known filmmakers such as Ouedraogo, Kabore, Yameogo, and Kouyate make popular television series. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_team.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Burkina_team.png/220px-Burkina_team.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Burkina_team.png/330px-Burkina_team.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Burkina_team.png/440px-Burkina_team.png 2x" data-file-width="3136" data-file-height="2232"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_team.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso_national_football_team" title="Burkina Faso national football team">Burkina Faso national football team</a> in white during a match
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Burkina_Faso" title="Sport in Burkina Faso">Sport in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Sport in Burkina Faso is widespread and includes football (soccer), basketball, cycling, rugby union, handball, tennis, boxing and martial arts. Football is the most popular sport in Burkina Faso, played both professionally, and informally in towns and villages across the country. The national team is nicknamed "Les Etalons" ("the Stallions") in reference to the legendary horse of Princess <a href="/wiki/Yennenga" title="Yennenga">Yennenga</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1998, Burkina Faso hosted the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> for which the Omnisport Stadium in Bobo-Dioulasso was built. Burkina Faso qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations">2013 African Cup of Nations</a> in South Africa and reached the final, but then lost to Nigeria 0-1. The country is currently ranked 53rd in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>, and has shown improvement in recent years, although they have never qualified for a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Basketball is another sport which enjoys much popularity for both men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Burkina Faso national basketball team">national team</a> had its most successful year in 2013 when it qualified for the <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket" title="AfroBasket">AfroBasket</a>, the continent's prime basketball event. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg/220px-Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg/330px-Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg/440px-Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="2160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burkina_Faso_media_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Burkinabé photographer at work in <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Burkina Faso">Media of Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Burkina_Faso" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in Burkina Faso">Communications in Burkina Faso</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The nation's principal media outlet is its state-sponsored combined television and radio service, <i>Radiodiffusion-Télévision Burkina</i> (RTB).<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <i>RTB</i> broadcasts on two <a href="/wiki/Medium-wave" class="mw-redirect" title="Medium-wave">medium-wave</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amplitude_modulation" title="Amplitude modulation">AM</a>) and several <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> frequencies. Besides RTB, there are privately owned sports, cultural, music, and religious FM radio stations. <i>RTB</i> maintains a worldwide short-wave news broadcast (<i>Radio Nationale Burkina</i>) in the French language from the capital at Ouagadougou using a 100&nbsp;kW transmitter on 4.815 and 5.030&nbsp;MHz.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Attempts to develop an independent press and media in Burkina Faso have been intermittent. In 1998, investigative journalist <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Zongo" title="Norbert Zongo">Norbert Zongo</a>, his brother Ernest, his driver, and another man were assassinated by unknown assailants, and the bodies burned. The crime was never solved.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-161">[161]</a></sup> However, an independent Commission of Inquiry later concluded that Norbert Zongo was killed for political reasons because of his investigative work into the death of David Ouedraogo, a chauffeur who worked for François Compaoré, President Blaise Compaoré's brother.<sup id="cite_ref-en.rsf.org_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.rsf.org-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Outrageous_Denial_of_Justice_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Outrageous_Denial_of_Justice-163">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 1999, François Compaoré was charged with the murder of David Ouedraogo, who had died as a result of torture in January 1998. The charges were later dropped by a military tribunal after an appeal. In August 2000, five members of the President's personal security guard detail (<i>Régiment de la Sécurité Présidentielle</i>, or RSP) were charged with the murder of Ouedraogo. RSP members Marcel Kafando, Edmond Koama, and Ousseini Yaro, investigated as suspects in the Norbert Zongo assassination, were convicted in the Ouedraogo case and sentenced to lengthy prison terms.<sup id="cite_ref-en.rsf.org_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.rsf.org-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Outrageous_Denial_of_Justice_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Outrageous_Denial_of_Justice-163">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the death of Norbert Zongo, several protests regarding the Zongo investigation and treatment of journalists have been prevented or dispersed by government police and security forces. In April 2007, popular radio reggae host <a href="/wiki/Sams%27K_Le_Jah" title="Sams'K Le Jah">Karim Sama</a>, whose programs feature reggae songs interspersed with critical commentary on alleged government injustice and corruption, received several death threats.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sama's personal car was later burned outside the private radio station <i>Ouaga FM</i> by unknown vandals.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> In response, the <a href="/wiki/Committee_to_Protect_Journalists" title="Committee to Protect Journalists">Committee to Protect Journalists</a> (CPJ) wrote to President Compaoré to request his government investigate the sending of e-mailed death threats to journalists and radio commentators in Burkina Faso who were critical of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-161">[161]</a></sup> In December 2008, police in Ouagadougou questioned leaders of a protest march that called for a renewed investigation into the unsolved Zongo assassination. Among the marchers was Jean-Claude Meda, the president of the Association of Journalists of Burkina Faso.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_festivals_and_events">Cultural festivals and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Cultural festivals and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Every two years, Ouagadougou hosts the <a href="/wiki/Panafrican_Film_and_Television_Festival_of_Ouagadougou" title="Panafrican Film and Television Festival of Ouagadougou">Panafrican Film and Television Festival of Ouagadougou</a> (FESPACO), the largest African cinema festival on the continent (February, odd years). </p>
      <p>Held every two years since 1988, the <a href="/wiki/International_Art_and_Craft_Fair,_Ouagadougou" class="mw-redirect" title="International Art and Craft Fair, Ouagadougou">International Art and Craft Fair, Ouagadougou</a> (SIAO), is one of Africa's most important trade shows for art and handicrafts (late October-early November, even years). </p>
      <p>Also every two years, the <a href="/wiki/Symposium_de_sculpture_sur_granit_de_Laongo" title="Symposium de sculpture sur granit de Laongo">Symposium de sculpture sur granit de Laongo</a> takes place on a site located about 35 kilometres (22 miles) from <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, in the province of <a href="/wiki/Oubritenga" class="mw-redirect" title="Oubritenga">Oubritenga</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Culture_Week_of_Burkina_Faso" title="National Culture Week of Burkina Faso">National Culture Week of Burkina Faso</a>, better known by its French name La Semaine Nationale de la culture (SNC), is one of the most important cultural activities of Burkina Faso. It is a biennial event which takes place every two years in Bobo Dioulasso, the second-largest city in the country. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Festival_International_des_Masques_et_des_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival International des Masques et des Arts">Festival International des Masques et des Arts</a> (FESTIMA), celebrating <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_masks" title="Traditional African masks">traditional masks</a>, is held every two years in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9dougou" title="Dédougou">Dédougou</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wreckage_of_a_dam_(Dourtenga,_2008).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg/220px-Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg/330px-Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg/440px-Wreckage_of_a_dam_%28Dourtenga%2C_2008%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wreckage_of_a_dam_(Dourtenga,_2008).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Damage caused by the Dourtenga floods in 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geographic and environmental causes can also play a significant role in contributing to Burkina Faso's issue of food insecurity.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> As the country is situated in the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> region, Burkina Faso experiences some of the most radical climatic variation in the world, ranging from severe flooding to extreme drought.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The unpredictable climatic shock that Burkina Faso citizens often face results in strong difficulties in being able to rely on and accumulate wealth through agricultural means.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Burkina Faso's climate also renders its crops vulnerable to insect attacks, including attacks from <a href="/wiki/Locust" title="Locust">locusts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket_(insect)" title="Cricket (insect)">crickets</a>, which destroy crops and further inhibit food production.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Not only is most of the population of Burkina Faso dependent on agriculture as a source of income, but they also rely on the agricultural sector for food that will directly feed the household.<sup id="cite_ref-Coping_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coping-171">[171]</a></sup> Due to the vulnerability of agriculture, more and more families are having to look for other sources of non-farm income,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> and often have to travel outside of their regional zone to find work.<sup id="cite_ref-Coping_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coping-171">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Issues">Other Issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Other Issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>On July 8, 2020, the United States raised concerns after an <a href="/wiki/HRW" class="mw-redirect" title="HRW">HRW</a> report revealed mass graves of at least 180 bodies, which have been found in northern Burkina Faso where soldiers are fighting jihadists.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Burkina_Faso&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

         <li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.wdl.org/en/item/635/">More (Language of the Mossi Tribe) Phrase Book</a> – "Burkina Faso is a former French colony, which became the independent state of Upper Volta in 1960.            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-85613-582-9" title="Special:BookSources/1-85613-582-9">1-85613-582-9</a>.          <li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFManning1998" class="citation book cs1">Manning, Patrick (1998). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=i4bPWSPutYcC"><i>Francophone Sub-Saharan Africa: 1880–1995</i></a>. Cambridge: Cambridge University Press. p.&nbsp;126. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780521645195" title="Special:BookSources/9780521645195"><bdi>9780521645195</bdi></a>. <q>The name of the country was chnged to Burkina Faso, and Sankara launched it on an aggressive, populist program of self-help.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Francophone+Sub-Saharan+Africa%3A+1880%E2%80%931995&amp;rft.place=Cambridge&amp;rft.pages=126&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.isbn=9780521645195&amp;rft.aulast=Manning&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrick&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Di4bPWSPutYcC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABurkina+Faso" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The name is an <a href="/wiki/Amalgamation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amalgamation (linguistics)">amalgam</a> of <a href="/wiki/More_language" class="mw-redirect" title="More language">More</a> <i>burkina</i> ("honest", "upright", or "incorruptible men") and <a href="/wiki/Dioula_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Dioula language">Jula</a> <i>faso</i> ("homeland"; literally "father's house"). The "-be" suffix in the name for the people – Burkinabe – comes from the Fula plural suffix for people, <i>-ɓe</i>.</span> </li>
